## How to Create a Robust Health and Safety Policy - First Aid and Fire Safety

Source: https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/blog/create-a-robust-health-and-safety-policy/

Skip to content
		
					
						
					
			
						
				
									**Tel:** +27 10 592 2111&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; **Email:** sales@firstaidfiresafety.co.za								
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
							
			
												
									
								
					Search
					
										
											
									
			
		
						
				
					
		
					
		
		
					
		
				
				
											
							
											
				
				
		
				&quot;,&quot;library&quot;:&quot;fa-solid&quot;},&quot;full_width&quot;:&quot;stretch&quot;,&quot;layout&quot;:&quot;horizontal&quot;,&quot;toggle&quot;:&quot;burger&quot;}" data-widget_type="nav-menu.default">
				
					
					
						
				
				
					
				
				
				
			
					
		
				
				
					# How to Create a Robust Health and Safety Policy
				
				
				
				
							
								
						
											
															
									
										Tanja Herrmannsen					
									
				
				
						
											
															
									
										June 11, 2024					
									
				
				
						
				
				
					
				
		
					
		
				
				
							
			
				Table of Contents			
							
				
					
		
			
							
		
						
				
				
		
					
		
					
				
				
When we think about a workplace buzzing with activity, the first thing that should come to mind is the safety and well-being of those who make it all happen: the employees. In South Africa, the [Occupational Health and Safety Act](https://www.labour.gov.za/DocumentCenter/Publications/Occupational%20Health%20and%20Safety/What%20every%20worker%20should%20know%20about%20health%20and%20safety%20at%20work.pdf?platform=hootsuite#:~:text=The%20Occupational%20Health%20and%20Safety%20Act%2C%201993%2C%20requires%20the%20employer,the%20health%20of%20the%20workers.) (OHS Act) clearly mandates that all employers have a strong health and safety policy in place. This policy is a framework to ensure that everyone works in an environment that values their health and livelihood. So, whether you’re starting from scratch or refining an existing policy, let’s look at how you can create a robust health and safety policy that not only meets but exceeds the basic requirements, safeguarding your team’s wellness and your organisation’s future.

## Defining Your health and safety policy

A health and safety policy, simply put, is your written commitment to managing risks and ensuring a safe working environment. It’s the backbone of safety in the workplace and serves as a clear guide for everyone from management to the newest recruit. To make it effective, your policy must clearly state who it covers – and that’s everyone under your roof, without exception.&nbsp;
However, it’s more than just a list of rules. A good policy anticipates scenarios where standard procedures might not be feasible and provides backup plans. For instance, if someone can’t follow a safety procedure due to unforeseen circumstances, what should they do? Your policy should have that answer.
Additionally, clarity is key. Use straightforward language to outline examples of what’s acceptable and what’s not. For example, you could spell out the rules concerning alcohol consumption, stating a zero-tolerance stance on working under the influence. By defining your policy with well-explained, relatable scenarios, you ensure that everyone understands and can follow it, making for a healthier and safer workplace.
## The core of your health and safety policy: The statement and plan

At the heart of your health and safety policy is the policy statement—a signed commitment from your CEO or Director that sets the tone for safety in your organisation. It’s not just a formality but a public declaration of your company’s dedication to safeguarding its people. This signed document should be on proud display where all employees can see it, reinforcing the message that health and safety are paramount.Beyond the statement lies the comprehensive [health and safety plan](https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/blog/health-and-safety-plan/), detailing the how-tos of your policy. It’s a blueprint for action that covers everything from personal protective equipment to emergency procedures and regular risk assessments. This plan is where you document the steps and strategies to create a healthy and safe workplace, addressing potential hazards and establishing protocols for safe work practices.Remember, your plan isn’t just a static document but a living one. It should evolve through regular updates and improvements, reflecting changes in regulations, new technologies, or different working procedures. And to ensure that it’s not just paperwork, it needs to be understood and followed by everyone. From training and supervision to continual improvement, your health and safety plan must be a clear, actionable, and dynamic tool in managing health and safety.

## Communication and understanding

The best health and safety policy is only as good as the understanding of those who implement it. It’s crucial to express your policy through clear, straightforward language. Avoid jargon that might confuse — your goal is for every single person, regardless of their role or literacy level, to grasp the contents fully and know what’s expected of them.
Effective communication also means actively overcoming language barriers within the organisation. It may involve translating the policy into other languages spoken by your workforce or using visual aids and symbols that can be universally understood. It’s about ensuring that everyone’s on the same page, quite literally.
Workshops, training sessions, and regular meetings can play a significant role in reinforcing the health and safety message. Encourage questions, provide clarifications, and make sure that everyone feels competent to act according to the policy. After all, a policy that lives in a drawer is of no use to anyone. It needs to be in the minds and actions of your employees to truly make a difference.
## The joint effort of management and employees

Creating a safe workplace is a team effort that requires active participation and commitment from both management and employees. The OHS committee, a [mix of representatives](https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/health-safety-training/) from various levels of the company, is the driving force behind this collaborative approach. This committee doesn’t just distribute information but fosters a culture of safety, where everyone feels responsible and empowered to contribute to a healthier and safer work environment.
Management’s role involves providing the necessary resources, setting clear expectations, and leading by example when it comes to health and safety practices. They must ensure that the working environment complies with safety regulations, conduct regular risk assessments, and create avenues for continual improvement.
Employees, on the other hand, are the eyes and ears on the ground. They are responsible for following the laid-out procedures, using personal protective equipment properly, and reporting any unsafe conditions or incidents. It’s essential that they understand their role in maintaining a safe workspace and feel confident to voice concerns without fear of repercussions.
This shared responsibility is the bedrock of a robust health and safety culture, where everyone works towards the common goal of preventing harm and promoting well-being.

## Compliance: Following the rules and understanding the risks

Abiding by the [OHS Act](https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/health-safety-training/the-occupational-health-safety-act/) isn’t just about dodging legal bullets; it’s fundamentally about respecting the right to a safe workplace. Compliance with health and safety legislation is a shared duty, both for the protection of individuals and the collective success of the organisation. A solid understanding of what the Act requires — for instance, the necessity for risk assessments, safe work practices, and the use of personal protective equipment — helps everyone recognise their part in creating a healthy and safe workplace.
But it’s not just about following rules; it’s about understanding why they matter. Everyone should be aware of the [risks of non-compliance](https://www.hellocontract.co.za/blog/enforcing-the-south-african-health-and-safety-act:-penalties-and-sanctions-for-non-compliance/), which can range from minor incidents to severe accidents, potentially leading to legal action, financial loss, or worse, harm to human life. Highlighting these risks within your policy and training ensures that health and safety are not taken lightly but seen as vital to personal and organisational well-being.
It is crucial to have procedures in place for updating your policies, ensuring they evolve with changes in legislation, technology, and working environments. Regular training and consultation with your team are also vital, fostering a workplace where health and safety matters are openly discussed and continually improved upon. By ingraining these values into your company culture, you not only comply with the law but also show a genuine commitment to the well-being of your most valuable asset — your people.
## Conclusion

In wrapping up, crafting a robust health and safety policy is not merely an onerous task—it’s a vital investment in the welfare of your team and the longevity of your business. By outlining clear procedures, ensuring effective communication, and fostering a culture of mutual commitment, you lay the groundwork for not just a legally compliant workplace, but one where safety and well-being are woven into its very DNA.
Reflect on your current health and safety policies: Do they truly serve your people and comply with the OHS Act? If you see room for improvement, remember, it’s never too late to enhance your approach. While generic resources like policy templates can offer a starting point, nothing compares to tailored, expert guidance.
At FAFST (First Aid, Fire, and Safety Training), we specialise in interpreting the nuances of the OHS Act and creating policies that are practical and compliant. More than just meeting legal requirements, we help foster a culture that prioritises health and safety at its core. To solidify your understanding and application of these vital regulations, consider enrolling in our OHS Act Course. This course is designed to equip you with knowledge and practical skills to maintain a safer, healthier workplace.
Don’t hesitate—[enroll in our OHS Act Course today](https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/health-safety-training/the-occupational-health-safety-act/) and take a significant step towards a safer, healthier workplace for everyone.

## What is a SHE Representative? - First Aid and Fire Safety

Source: https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/blog/what-is-a-she-representative/

Skip to content
		
					
						
					
			
						
				
									**Tel:** +27 10 592 2111&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; **Email:** sales@firstaidfiresafety.co.za								
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
							
			
												
									
								
					Search
					
										
											
									
			
		
						
				
					
		
					
		
		
					
		
				
				
											
							
											
				
				
		
				&quot;,&quot;library&quot;:&quot;fa-solid&quot;},&quot;full_width&quot;:&quot;stretch&quot;,&quot;layout&quot;:&quot;horizontal&quot;,&quot;toggle&quot;:&quot;burger&quot;}" data-widget_type="nav-menu.default">
				
					
					
						
				
				
					
				
				
				
			
					
		
				
				
					# What is a SHE Representative?
				
				
				
				
							
								
						
											
															
									
										Niell Truter					
									
				
				
						
											
															
									
										June 13, 2024					
									
				
				
						
				
				
					
				
		
					
		
				
				
							
			
				Table of Contents			
							
				
					
		
			
							
		
						
				
				
		
					
		
					
				
				
A SHE Representative, also known as a SHE Rep, is an individual appointed within the workplace to represent their fellow employees in ensuring all risks and hazards are identified and managed as reasonably practicable. The SHE Rep consults with and makes representations to the employer in the Health and Safety Committee on matters affecting safety, health, and welfare. This role is crucial for maintaining a safe work environment, protecting not just employees but any other person affected by workplace activities. Sections 17 and 18 of the [Occupational Health &amp; Safety (OHS) Act](https://www.gov.za/sites/default/files/gcis_document/201409/act85of1993.pdf) detail the appointments and functions of SHE Reps.

## Who is eligible to be a SHE Rep and how many are needed?

Per Section 17(4) of the OHS Act, candidates for the SHE Rep role must be full-time employees familiar with the conditions and activities, including the risks and hazards of their specific work areas. The appointment must be documented, and the duration agreed upon by both employer and Health &amp; Safety Representative. Employers cannot arbitrarily appoint any employee or new hire to this role; it requires a nomination process.
In workplaces with over 20 employees, one SHE Rep is needed for every group of 50 employees in general industry and 1:100 for shops and offices. According to the Mine Health and Safety Act 29 of 1996, every mine with more than 20 employees must appoint a Health &amp; Safety Representative for each shift at each designated working place.
## How does the appointment process work?

The General Administrative Regulations Section 6 of the OHS Act stipulates that employers must engage with registered trade unions when appointing a Health and Safety Representative. In the absence of a registered trade union, employers must consult with employees to agree on the following:

The nomination or election process for the SHE Rep.
The terms of office and the removal process for underperformance.
The procedure for filling vacancies.
The duties of the Health and Safety Representative as outlined in the OHS Act.
The facilities, [training](https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/health-safety-training/health-safety-representative/), and support necessary for the SHE Rep to fulfil their duties under Section 18 of the OHS Act.

## Why must a Health &amp; Safety Representative be appointed by a nomination process?

The SHE Rep position does not come with additional remuneration and should be filled by someone with a genuine interest in health and safety, respected by peers. Nomination ensures the chosen individual is someone employees look up to and can easily follow instructions from, regarding health and safety. Importantly, nominees must accept the role, ensuring they are willing and capable of performing the required duties.
## What are the duties of a SHE Representative?

A SHE Rep, or Safety, Health, and Environmental Representative, plays a crucial role in ensuring [workplace safety](https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/blog/workplace-safety/) and compliance with health and safety regulations. Here are the primary duties of a SHE Rep:
**Reviewing safety measures:**

SHE Reps regularly assess the effectiveness of health and safety measures in their designated workspaces. This includes identifying any shortcomings and suggesting improvements.

**Identifying hazards:**

One of the core responsibilities is to identify potential hazards within the workplace. This proactive approach helps in preventing accidents and ensuring a safe working environment.

**Examining incident causes:**

SHE Reps investigate the causes of workplace incidents. By understanding what went wrong, they can recommend measures to prevent future occurrences.

**Investigating complaints:**

Employees may raise concerns regarding health and safety. The SHE Rep investigates these complaints to ensure they are addressed promptly and effectively.

**Making representations:**

SHE Reps make representations to the employer about health and safety issues. If the employer does not address these issues, the SHE Rep can escalate them to an inspector.

**Accompanying inspectors:**

During official inspections, SHE Reps accompany inspectors and participate in consultations. This ensures that the inspections are thorough and all safety concerns are addressed.

**Receiving information:**

SHE Reps receive information from inspectors as outlined in Section 36 of the OHS Act. This information is vital for maintaining and improving safety standards.

**Participating in safety committee meetings:**

As members of the health and safety committee, SHE Reps attend regular meetings to discuss and address ongoing safety issues within the workplace.

### Rights of a SHE Rep:

Site visits:

SHE Reps have the right to visit the site of an incident at reasonable times and attend inspections.

Document inspection:

They can inspect documents maintained by the employer in accordance with the OHS Act to perform their duties.

Technical assistance:

With employer approval, SHE Reps can be accompanied by a technical adviser during inspections.

Internal audits:

They participate in any internal health and safety audits.

Training requirements:

All activities related to the designation, duties, and training of SHE Reps must be completed during normal working hours.&nbsp;

Additional training:

Beyond the basic SHE Rep course, additional training such as Incident Investigation, [Hazard Identification and Risk Assessment (HIRA)](https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/health-safety-training/hazard-identification-and-risk-assessment-hira/) would benefit the SHE Rep.

## When should a Health &amp; Safety Representative carry out their functions and what training is required?

All tasks related to the designation, duties, and training of SHE Reps must occur during normal working hours. Employers cannot expect representatives to perform these duties after hours or use their leave for training purposes.
The Health and Safety Representative course provides essential knowledge for SHE Reps to perform their roles. Additional training and courses addressing specific workplace risks (e.g Stacking &amp; Storage, [HAZMAT](https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/specialised-training/hazardous-material-handling-hazmat/)) can significantly enhance their effectiveness.

## Can a Health &amp; Safety Representative incur civil liability?

Under Section 18(4) of the OHS Act, SHE Reps are shielded from civil liability for failing to perform any required duty under the Act. This protection ensures they cannot be sued for negligence in fulfilling their functions as outlined by the OHS Act. However, this immunity applies only to their official duties; any misconduct outside this scope could still result in civil or criminal liability.
## Conclusion

The role of a Health and Safety Representative, or SHE Rep, is fundamental in promoting and maintaining a safe work environment. By ensuring all risks and hazards are identified and managed, SHE Reps play a critical part in workplace safety, safeguarding employees and anyone else affected by workplace activities. The appointment process, as detailed in the OHS Act, emphasises the importance of selecting suitable candidates through a [nomination process](https://labourguide.co.za/health-and-safety/workplace-health-and-safety-representatives#:~:text=Workplace%20health%20and%20safety%20representatives%20play%20a%20crucial%20role%20in%20this%20regard.&amp;text=Section%2017%20of%20the%20Occupational,representatives%20for%20the%20said%20workplace.) to ensure they have the necessary commitment and respect from their peers.
SHE Reps have a range of duties and responsibilities, from reviewing safety measures to participating in inspections and investigations. They must perform these functions during regular working hours and are protected from civil liability while carrying out their duties under the OHS Act. However, they must act responsibly within the scope of their role to avoid any personal legal repercussions.
By understanding the significance of the SHE Rep role, employers can ensure they have effective health and safety representatives who are well-equipped through appropriate training to maintain a safe working environment. Comprehensive training courses, including basic SHE Rep courses and specialised training like Incident Investigation and HIRA, are crucial in equipping SHE Reps to handle their responsibilities effectively.
For more information on SHE Rep courses, [SHE Rep training](https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/health-safety-training/health-safety-representative/), and other related queries such as the SHE Rep course price, contact us today. By investing in proper training and a robust appointment process, organisations can foster a culture of safety and compliance, benefiting all employees.
				
				
					
				
					
				
					
				
		
					
				
				
							
					
					
						
					
			
					
						
				
					Ready to start your training?

## The Role of Human Resources in Workplace Safety - First Aid and Fire Safety

Source: https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/blog/human-resources-in-workplace-safety/

Skip to content
		
					
						
					
			
						
				
									**Tel:** +27 10 592 2111&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; **Email:** sales@firstaidfiresafety.co.za								
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
							
			
												
									
								
					Search
					
										
											
									
			
		
						
				
					
		
					
		
		
					
		
				
				
											
							
											
				
				
		
				&quot;,&quot;library&quot;:&quot;fa-solid&quot;},&quot;full_width&quot;:&quot;stretch&quot;,&quot;layout&quot;:&quot;horizontal&quot;,&quot;toggle&quot;:&quot;burger&quot;}" data-widget_type="nav-menu.default">
				
					
					
						
				
				
					
				
				
				
			
					
		
				
				
					# The Role of Human Resources in Workplace Safety
				
				
				
				
							
								
						
											
															
									
										Malcolm Midgely					
									
				
				
						
											
															
									
										June 20, 2024					
									
				
				
						
				
				
					
				
		
					
		
				
				
							
			
				Table of Contents			
							
				
					
		
			
							
		
						
				
				
		
					
		
					
				
				
In South Africa, the importance of [workplace safety](https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/blog/workplace-safety/) is underscored by the [Occupational Health and Safety (OHS) Act 85 of 1993](https://www.gov.za/sites/default/files/gcis_document/201409/act85of1993.pdf), which mandates organisations to maintain high safety standards. Human Resources (HR) departments play a crucial role in this regard, evolving from administrative functions to becoming strategic partners in ensuring a safe working environment.

## Understanding Human Resource Management (HRM)

### What is Human Resource Management?

**Human Resource Management** (HRM) is a strategic approach to the effective management of people in a company to help the business gain a competitive advantage. It is designed to maximise employee performance and is primarily concerned with managing people within organisations, focusing on policies and systems.
Human Resource Management Definition: Human Resources (HR) is responsible for managing the workforce, focusing on systems and policies such as recruitment, training, and compliance with safety laws.
Human Resources Definition: HR refers to the department within an organisation that is tasked with managing employees, implementing company policies, and ensuring that the workplace is safe and productive.
### Functions of Human Resource Management

The functions of human resources include recruitment, training and development, performance management, and ensuring compliance with safety regulations. HRM ensures that all employees understand and follow established safety protocols, thus playing a critical role in workplace safety.
## Key Roles of Human Resources in enhancing workplace safety

### Compliance with the OHS Act 85 of 1993

HR departments ensure compliance with the OHS Act by developing and implementing safety policies and [training programs.](https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/) This includes:
**Policy formulation:** Establishing clear safety guidelines and emergency protocols.
**Training implementation:** Conducting essential safety training sessions, including first aid, fire safety, and regulatory compliance.
**Monitoring and reporting:** Keeping accurate records of incidents and training sessions to ensure ongoing compliance with OHS regulations.
### Comprehensive safety training programs managed by HR

#### Talent management and succession planning

Succession planning is crucial in ensuring that critical safety knowledge and responsibilities are passed down, maintaining a continuity of safety standards.
#### Employee training and development

HR leads training initiatives to keep the workforce updated on the latest safety standards and practices, including:
**[First Aid training:](https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/first-aid-training-courses/)** Employees are equipped with life-saving skills, enhancing their ability to respond to workplace emergencies promptly.
**[Fire Safety training:](https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/fire-fighting-training/)** Comprehensive training on [fire prevention](https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/blog/fire-prevention-tactics/), emergency response, and the proper use of fire extinguishers using the PASS method.
**Safety [Compliance training](https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/blog/legal-liability-training/):** Ensuring that all employees are familiar with industry-specific regulations and understand their roles in maintaining workplace safety.
### The impact of training on workplace safety

Effective safety training programs significantly reduce the risk of workplace accidents and ensure that employees are prepared for emergencies. These programs include regular drills, refresher courses, and practical sessions on using emergency equipment.

## Building a culture of safety through HR

### Fostering a safe work environment

HR plays a pivotal role in creating a culture of safety where employees feel empowered to report potential hazards. Regular communication and transparent policies contribute to this environment, encouraging a proactive approach to workplace safety.
### Engaging employees through learning and development

Engaged employees are more likely to adhere to safety guidelines and contribute positively to maintaining a safe work environment. HR uses learning and development programs to keep employees informed and engaged.
## Leveraging technology for enhanced safety management

### Human Resource Information Systems (HRIS)

HRIS technology helps HR professionals manage training records, monitor compliance, and track employee progress. This technological support is vital for ensuring that safety standards are consistently met across the organisation.
## HR’s strategic role in emergency preparedness

Human Resources is not only tasked with managing day-to-day safety protocols but also with preparing for emergencies. This preparation involves creating detailed emergency response plans, conducting regular drills, and ensuring that all employees are aware of their roles during an emergency.
### Emergency response planning

HR is responsible for developing comprehensive emergency response plans that outline procedures for various scenarios, such as fires, natural disasters, or workplace violence. These plans are designed to minimise confusion and ensure a swift and coordinated response.
### Regular drills and simulations

To ensure that employees are prepared for emergencies, HR conducts regular drills and simulations. These exercises help to reinforce the procedures outlined in the emergency response plans and ensure that employees are familiar with the actions they need to take.
### Collaboration with other Departments

HR’s role in workplace safety is often collaborative, requiring coordination with and input from other departments such as Operations, Legal, and Facilities Management. HR works closely with Operations to understand the specific safety risks associated with different roles and environments. Collaboration with the Legal department ensures that all safety policies are compliant with current laws and regulations. Facilities Management is involved in maintaining safe physical environments and equipment.
### Creating a unified safety strategy

By collaborating with other departments, HR can create a unified safety strategy that addresses all aspects of workplace safety. This comprehensive approach ensures that safety protocols are integrated into every part of the organisation, from daily operations to long-term strategic planning.
## Measuring the effectiveness of safety programs

HR is also responsible for measuring the effectiveness of safety programs to ensure continuous improvement.

### Key Performance Indicators (KPIs)

HR uses KPIs to track the success of safety initiatives. These indicators may include the number of workplace accidents, the frequency of safety training sessions, and employee compliance rates. Regular analysis of these metrics helps HR identify areas for improvement and adjust strategies as needed.
### Employee feedback

Gathering feedback from employees is another important aspect of measuring safety program effectiveness. HR conducts surveys and focus groups to understand employees’ perceptions of workplace safety and gather suggestions for improvement. This feedback is invaluable for creating a safer and more responsive work environment.
## Conclusion: HR’s central role in workplace safety

Human Resources departments are essential in building and maintaining a safety-conscious culture within organisations. By prioritising comprehensive safety training and strategic planning, HR ensures that all employees are well-prepared to handle emergencies and contribute to a safe working environment. From the implementation of rigorous training programs to the strategic development of company culture, HR professionals are indispensable allies in fostering workplace safety under the framework of the [OHS Act 85 of 1993.](https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/health-safety-training/the-occupational-health-safety-act/)
HR’s strategic role in workplace safety extends beyond compliance and training. It involves fostering a culture of safety, leveraging technology, collaborating with other departments, and continuously measuring and improving safety programs. By taking a holistic and proactive approach, HR can ensure that workplace safety is ingrained in every aspect of the organisation, creating a safer and more productive environment for all employees.

## Specialised Training - First Aid and Fire Safety

Source: https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/specialised-training/

# **Specialised H&amp;S Courses**
First Aid Fire and Safety Training presents a range of specialised courses to fulfil our clients’ specific health &amp; safety compliance obligations. These courses are condensed into 1-day sessions, minimizing disruption to work while delivering crucial knowledge and abilities.								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
			
						
		
						
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
						
				
				
				
					We Offer Accredited Health and Safety Specialised Training 
				
				
				
				
									Our course variety allows our clients to select the best option for their health and safety teams, ensuring they have the required knowledge and abilities to effectively perform their vital health and safety duties.								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
					Specialised Courses
				
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
					## Evacuation Planning
				
				
				
				
									The purpose of this training is to prepare the health and safety personnel for an unanticipated evacuation of the workplace through simulated drills and running through the full evacuation procedure. This encompasses preparing beforehand, assigning duties, and complying with legal requirements by conducting&nbsp; evacuation drills twice per year. 								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Training
					
					
				
								
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
																														
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
																														
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
					HAZMAT
				
				
				
				
									The presence of hazardous materials or chemicals is a common occurrence in most work environments and job sites, ranging from low-volume and low-toxicity to large amounts with high toxicity to both human health and the environment. To minimise the consequences of any incidents, employers should have some members of their health and safety team receive specialized training from a health and safety training provider on how to handle these hazardous materials.								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Training
					
					
				
								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
					Stacking and Storage
				
				
				
				
									Having a well-implemented and maintained system for stacking and storing items is crucial in all work settings. A properly managed and controlled environment allows for efficient inventory management, limits unnecessary expenses, promotes a clean and organised work environment, and decreases the chances of accidents and fires.								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Training
					
					
				
								
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
																														
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
																														
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
					HIV AIDS Awareness 
				
				
				
				
									HIV, or the Human Immunodeficiency Virus, is a widespread epidemic that has impacted millions globally. The virus undermines the body’s defences, leading to the development of AIDS, which is characterised by a decline in immunity and a strengthening of the virus.								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Training
					
					
				
								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
					First Aid, Fire and Evacuation Responder Skills Program 
				
				
				
				
									The three accredited courses that comprise this skills program are a vital component of a company’s legal training requirements for health and safety. The 5-day program provides both hands-on and theoretical instruction in areas such as first aid, firefighting basics, and emergency evacuation planning. To get verification and endorsement, a participant must complete and submit a workplace assignment through the HWSETA site, which can take 4-6 months. Upon completion, only periodic refresher courses are necessary, as the certificate has lifetime validity.

## Hazardous Material Handling (HAZMAT) - First Aid and Fire Safety

Source: https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/specialised-training/hazardous-material-handling-hazmat/

# **Hazardous Material Handling (HAZMAT)**
According to the Hazardous Chemical Substance Regulations of the Occupational Health and Safety Act 85 of 1993, an employer must provide their employees with the proper information and training before any potential exposure to HAZMAT so they can respond appropriately and correctly.								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Now 
					
					
				
								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
			
						
		
						
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
						
				
				
				
					## Course Overview
				
				
				
				
									A HAZMAT chemical spill or leak can have significant and lasting harm to humans, animals, and the environment. It’s crucial to know the appropriate materials and equipment to use, protective clothing requirements, and effective management of hazardous materials after cleanup. The effects of HAZMAT on humans and the environment can vary depending on the properties and hazard class of the spilt material.								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
						
				
				
				
					Book Your Training Today

					About HAZMAT Course
				
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
						
					
			
						
				
							
			
		
						
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
					#### Course Information
				
				
				
				
							
			
						
		
						
				
				
				
									

Duration

HAZMAT is a 1-day course.

Cost

The cost of the course is R825.00, exclusive of VAT.

**Certification**

Upon successful completion of the 1-day course, delegates will receive a certificate valid for 2 years.

**Venues**

Training can be held on-premises at your organisation with a minimum of 8 attendees, or at one of our designated training centres located in Johannesburg North, Durban, Port Elizabeth, or Cape Town.

								
				
					
		
					
		
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
						
					
			
						
				
							
			
		
						
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
					What We Offer
				
				
				
				
							
			
						
		
						
				
				
				
					Course Content and Modules
				
				
				
				
							
							
										Introduction and Classification of Dangerous Goods - Understanding the distinctions between hazardous chemicals has been made simpler with the use of tools like MSDS, TREM Cards, Hazardous Labels, and Dangerous Goods Placards.
									
								
										Hazards Associated with Dangerous Goods  - The effects of HAZMAT varies on humans, animals, and the environment. This course covers the various ways these dangerous chemicals can enter the human body.
									
								
										Personal Protective Equipment - Personal Protective Equipment (PPE) is critical in ensuring worker safety. Employers must provide the appropriate safety gear, and employees must understand how to properly use and wear it.
									
								
										Safe Handling and Flammable Substances - Some HAZMAT is flammable and can pose a risk of fire. Workers must be trained on how to safely handle and store these materials.
									
								
										Spillage Control - In the event of a spill, everyone needs to understand the proper procedures to control it and prevent further harm.
									
								
										Formulating a Response Plan - A response plan outlines the policies and procedures for employees to follow in the case of a HAZMAT spill.

					## Course Overview

This includes providing them with the necessary information and training to guarantee their health and safety. Staff training on effective stacking and storage methods is crucial in any workplace where these activities are carried out.

										Fire safety – In a warehouse where a lot of materials are kept fires may easily erupt with catastrophic results. The need for good housekeeping is discussed along with the importance of a fire prevention programme in the workplace.

# **Evacuation Planning**
Being prepared for emergencies and disasters is crucial, as they can happen unexpectedly, anywhere, at any moment. To ensure the safety of yourself and your business, it’s important to have a well-prepared evacuation plan. This course is designed to assist you in planning for these unforeseen events.								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Now 
					
					
				
								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
			
						
		
						
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
						
				
				
				
					## Course Overview
				
				
				
				
									It’s essential to understand the importance of safety in the workplace and know when to stop any procedure if you feel unsafe. This course focuses on emergency preparedness and the importance of conducting regular evacuation drills in the workplace.Upon completing the course, delegates will have a thorough understanding of conducting mock evacuation drills, creating evacuation floor plans, identifying key personnel responsibilities, calling for emergency interventions, and managing evacuations in various scenarios. This knowledge will enhance your ability to prepare for and respond to emergencies safely and efficiently.

Source: https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/first-aid-training-courses/

# **First Aid Courses**
Acquiring First Aid skills is a vital step towards ensuring your team’s safety.								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
			
						
		
						
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
						
				
				
				
					## We Offer Accredited First Aid Training
				
				
				
				
									At First Aid, Fire and Safety Training, we offer comprehensive and fully accredited first aid training courses. All study materials are included and the lessons are delivered by dynamic and competent instructors. The theory and practical exercises give learners a solid foundation of knowledge, skills and confidence to administer first aid in emergency situations 								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
					First Aid Courses
				
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
					First Aid NQF Level 1
				
				
				
				
									This accredited course covers emergency first aid such as CPR, AED use, choking, shock and seizures. In addition, the course includes first aid treatment for heart attacks, stroke, asthma and traumatic injuries such as chest, abdominal, head and spinal injuries.								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Training

The course incorporates extensive simulations and hands-on experience to enhance participants’ competence in delivering advanced first aid.								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Training
					
					
				
								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
					## CPR for Everyone 
				
				
				
				
									Cardiopulmonary Resuscitation (CPR) is a critical life-saving skill that every individual should be familiar with. By performing CPR, one can help maintain vital organ function until professional assistance arrives. Our CPR courses cover the latest global CPR, choking first aid, and Automated External Defibrillator (AED) protocols for adults, children, and infants. To promote widespread knowledge and training in CPR, we offer the option to arrange a course for a group of 8 delegates at either your workplace or one of our training venues.								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Training
					
					
				
								
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
																														
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
																														
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
					## CPR for Professionals 
				
				
				
				
									Cardiopulmonary Resuscitation (CPR) is a lifesaving skill that all healthcare professionals are taught and know how to perform, but unfortunately don’t get the opportunity to practice in real life, or in a training environment. This CPR course is designed by the Resuscitation Council of SA for professionals and has a different and more flexible approach to the CPR training workshop, compared to the normal BLS for Healthcare Providers.&nbsp;&nbsp;								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Training
					
					
				
								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
					## BLS for Healthcare Providers
				
				
				
				
									The popular CPR course covers the latest global CPR, choking first aid, and AED (automated external defibrillator) protocols for adults, children, and infants. It is the ideal course for all healthcare professionals to attend to revise and refresh the latest BLS resuscitation trends and protocols, practice CPR and sharpen their skills. We also offer CPR for Professionals which is very similar to BLS for Healthcare Providers but is accredited by the Resuscitation Council of South Africa.

Source: https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/first-aid-training-courses/bls-for-healthcare-providers-5-hours/

# **BLS for Healthcare Providers**
The Basic Life Support (BLS) for Healthcare Providers program provides a comprehensive and updated overview of the latest global resuscitation trends, skills, and protocols. This course is highly recommended for all healthcare professionals as it serves as an essential refresher for basic life support techniques.								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Now 
					
					
				
								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
			
						
		
						
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
						
				
				
				
					## Course Overview
				
				
				
				
									This Basic Life Support (BLS) course is of exceptional quality, conforming to the standards set by the American Heart Association. The course emphasises hands-on training in adult, child, and infant CPR through a favourable learner-to-equipment ratio. Participants can earn CPD points, which can be submitted to the Health Professions Council of South Africa every two years. The training can be conducted either at the healthcare facility or one of our venues, with a minimum of 8 attendees required per session.

## Health & Safety Training - First Aid and Fire Safety

Source: https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/health-safety-training/

# **Health and Safety Courses**
The Occupational Health &amp; Safety Act mandates health and safety training as an employer’s legal obligation.								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
			
						
		
						
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
						
				
				
				
					We Offer Accredited Health and Safety Training 
				
				
				
				
									First Aid and Fire Safety Training offers a comprehensive range of professional and accredited Occupational Health and Safety courses. These courses enable employers, employees, contractors, and the general public to understand and fulfil the requirements of the Occupational Health and Safety (OHS) Act No 85 of 1993.								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
					Health and Safety Courses
				
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
																														
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
					Health &amp; Safety Specialist
				
				
				
				
									This specialised course for Health and Safety Officers provides a comprehensive and logical understanding of the Occupational Health and Safety (OHS) Act and the environment. Ideal for individuals seeking to start a career in OHS and looking to effectively implement health and safety in the workplace, this course is one of our premier offerings and is highly recommended to all attendees and clients.								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Training
					
					
				
								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
					Health &amp; Safety Supervisor
				
				
				
				
									The Health and Safety Supervisor course is a two-day, comprehensive program designed for managers, department heads, and supervisors. This widely popular course provides specific training for supervisors and managers and covers key aspects of the Occupational Health and Safety Act, enabling them to understand and fulfil the requirements of health and safety compliance. The course delivers all the information clearly and concisely, emphasizing the critical elements of safety management.								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Training
					
					
				
								
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
																														
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
																														
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
					Health &amp; Safety Representative
				
				
				
				
									Health and Safety Representatives play a crucial role in a company’s approach to health and safety. They serve as advocates for employees at the quarterly health and safety committee meetings and work with management to promote a safe workplace. This course equips delegates with the skills necessary to serve as a representative in any work setting. It is a popular course due to the legal requirement for companies to have a Health and Safety Representative as outlined in the OHS Act.								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Training
					
					
				
								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
					Hazard Identification and Risk Assessment Course (HIRA)
				
				
				
				
									The Occupational Health and Safety (OHS) Act aims to identify health and safety hazards and risks in the workplace and to implement measures to eliminate or reduce these risks. This course provides training on how to attain a safe work environment and promote the overall health and well-being of all individuals in the workplace.								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Training
					
					
				
								
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
																														
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
																														
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
					## Occupational Health &amp; Safety Act
				
				
				
				
									Our Occupational Health and Safety (OHS) Act course focuses on providing an understanding of the key sections of the OHS Act 85 of 1993. It aims to increase delegates’ confidence and comprehension of the act, which can be intimidating and complex. Upon completing the course, delegates will have a clearer understanding of safety management within the act and will be better equipped to implement it with confidence.								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Training
					
					
				
								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
					16.2 Workshop 
				
				
				
				
									Our 16.2 Workshop is a concise 2-hour session designed for executives, employer reps, department heads, and supervisors with limited time. The goal of this interactive and engaging workshop is to provide a better understanding of the Occupational Health and Safety (OHS) act and to equip attendees with the knowledge necessary to ensure compliance within their organizations or departments.								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Training
					
					
				
								
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
																														
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
																														
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
					Incident Investigation 
				
				
				
				
									The incident investigation course equips the employee with the essential knowledge and skills to confidently and accurately conduct investigations.

## The Occupational Health & Safety Act – 1 Day - First Aid and Fire Safety

Source: https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/health-safety-training/the-occupational-health-safety-act/

# **The Occupational Health &amp; Safety Act**
The OHS Act 85 of 1993 requires employers and employees to take all necessary measures to establish a safe and healthy workplace. It also mandates that the CEO, management, supervisors, OHS representatives, and other employees understand their respective health and safety obligations in the work environment.								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Now 
					
					
				
								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
			
						
		
						
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
						
				
				
				
					## Course Overview
				
				
				
				
									Non-compliance with the OHS act can result in serious consequences, including fines, imprisonment, or both in extreme cases. To ensure a safer workplace for everyone, it is important to educate and train employees on this vital piece of legislation.Although the one-day course provides an overview of the OHS act, further training or self-study may be required to gain a complete understanding of the act’s complexities.

## Hazard Identification and Risk Assessment (HIRA) - 1 Day - First Aid and Fire Safety

Source: https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/health-safety-training/hazard-identification-and-risk-assessment-hira/

# **Hazard Identification and Risk Assessment (HIRA)**
Identifying hazards and assessing the associated risks assists companies in formulating a successful health &amp; safety plan								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Now 
					
					
				
								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
			
						
		
						
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
						
				
				
				
					## Course Overview
				
				
				
				
									A comprehensive health and safety risk management plan implements effective controls to reduce or eliminate hazards. Hazards that pose a low risk can also be addressed by management through mitigation or acceptance. Acquiring the skill of hazard identification and risk assessment is crucial, and our course gives delegates a thorough understanding and the necessary skills to perform risk assessments in the workplace.								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
						
				
				
				
					Book Your Training Today
				
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
																														
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
							
                
                        
                            
                        
                        First Name*Email*
                            
                        Preferred Month for Training*JanuaryFebruaryMarchAprilMayJuneJulyAugustSeptemberOctoberNovemberDecemberPhone Number*Location*Johannesburg NorthCape TownDurbanPort ElizabethOtherThis field is hidden when viewing the formTraining RequiredreCAPTCHA
          
            
            
            
            
            
            
            
            
            
            
        
                        
                        

						
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
					About the Hazard Identification and Risk Assessment Course
				
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
						
					
			
						
				
							
			
		
						
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
					#### Course Information
				
				
				
				
							
			
						
		
						
				
				
				
									**Duration**Hazard Identification Risk Assessment is a 1-day course.**Cost**The cost of the course is R925.00, exclusive of VAT.**Certification**Upon successfully finishing the 1-day program, delegates will receive a certificate which will be valid for 2 years.**Venues**The course can be facilitated on-site at your location if you have a minimum of 8 delegates, or at one of our training venues located in Johannesburg North, Durban, Port Elizabeth, or Cape Town.								
				
					
		
					
		
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
						
					
			
						
				
																														
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
					What We Offer
				
				
				
				
							
			
						
		
						
				
				
				
					Course Content and Modules
				
				
				
				
							
							
										The legal aspects of risk assessments covers the OHS Act laws related to risk assessments, including the differences between baseline, continuous, and issue-based assessments and the process of continuous risk assessments.
									
								
										The Importance of conducting risk assessments highlights the need for and the timing of conducting continuous risk assessments.
									
								
										Risk assessment documentation covers the different types of documentation used in risk assessments, such as checklists, planned task observation forms, and standard operating procedures.
									
								
										Common hazards and risks covers the common hazards and risks encountered during a continuous risk assessment in the workplace.
									
								
										Recording of findings emphasises the importance of recording the findings of a risk assessment to effectively communicate with the health and safety committee and the employer.
									
								
										Remedial and follow-up actions once the hazards and risks have been identified and ranked. This section covers the necessary actions the employer needs to take to improve the safety of the working environment by reducing, mitigating, or eliminating the hazards.

Source: https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/health-safety-training/health-safety-supervisor/

# **Health &amp; Safety Supervisor**
The two-day Health and Safety Supervisor course covers various aspects of the Occupational Health and Safety Act 85 of 1993, including its sections, requirements, and objectives.								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Now 
					
					
				
								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
			
						
		
						
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
						
				
				
				
					## Course Overview
				
				
				
				
									The CEO and executive team of a company are occupied with managing the business, leaving limited time to oversee health and safety compliance measures. To address this, Section 16.2 allows the CEO to appoint a health and safety supervisor, to handle health and safety within the workplace on their behalf. This appointment doesn’t absolve the CEO of accountability and liability according to the Act, but it grants them the authority to delegate health and safety management to a designated individual.

										Hazard Identification Risk Assessment (HIRA) training on how to conduct thorough health and safety risk assessments with the involvement of employees and representatives from various sections of the workplace. This process involves identifying hazards and risks, implementing suggested controls, and eliminating or reducing the likelihood of injury and illness in the workplace.
									
								
										Incident and accident investigations, which are an important aspect of health and safety management. The supervisor or manager must be part of the investigation team and work with management to investigate all incidents and accidents to prevent reoccurrence.

# **Health &amp; Safety Specialist**
Health &amp; Safety Officers play a key role in ensuring the safety of employees, visitors, and contractors within an organisation. They are accountable for creating and executing the health and safety plan and making sure it aligns with the Occupational Health and Safety (OHS) Act 85 of 1993 standards.								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Now 
					
					
				
								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
			
						
		
						
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
						
				
				
				
					## Course Overview
				
				
				
				
									Businesses and their management teams desire a sense of security regarding their Occupational Health and Safety (OHS) obligations, and the Health and Safety Officer provides that peace of mind. Research demonstrates that most incidents and accidents can be prevented by identifying and addressing potential hazards and risks from sources such as employee mistakes, faulty equipment, poor practices, etc. The Health and Safety Officer helps minimize this risk and decrease the likelihood of incidents, accidents, and health problems occurring.

# **Firefighting Courses**

					## We Offer Accredited Firefighting Training
				
				
				
				
									Protecting your workplace and employees from fire is critical. Our accredited firefighting courses provide comprehensive training in fire safety, prevention, and management, including hands-on experience with fire extinguishers. This training helps employees prevent and manage fire emergencies, reducing the risk of damage, downtime, and loss of life. Investing in firefighting training is a responsible management decision that meets legal requirements and minimises the impact of fire-related incidents.

Fire wardens play an important role in maintaining health and safety within organisations, and this course is a valuable tool in building their knowledge and skills.

## Firefighting - 1 Day - First Aid and Fire Safety

Source: https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/fire-fighting-training/fire-fighting-1/

# **Firefighting**
It is important to emphasise the significance of providing employees with basic firefighting training. In the event of a fire emergency, the initial actions taken by a trained firefighter in the first few crucial minutes can greatly impact the outcome. The proper handling of the situation can potentially contain the fire, preventing it from escalating into a fire emergency.								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Now 
					
					
				
								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
			
						
		
						
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
						
				
				
				
					## Course Overview
				
				
				
				
									This course equips your employees and health &amp; safety team members with the necessary firefighting skills to prevent or stop a fire from occurring. Some of the modules covered include the Fire Tetrahedron, common causes of fires, different classes of fires and the appropriate fire extinguishers to use, and roles and responsibilities of a fire warden.								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
						
				
				
				
					Book Your Training Today

## Advanced Firefighting – 2 Days - First Aid and Fire Safety

Source: https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/fire-fighting-training/advanced-fire-fighting/

# **Advanced Firefighting**
Every year, South Africa experiences a high number of fires that result in devastating loss of life and property damage worth billions of rand. To mitigate these risks, it is crucial to invest in advanced firefighting training for your company’s firefighting team and fire wardens. By doing so, you can ensure that they are equipped with the necessary skills and knowledge to effectively respond to and prevent fires in high-risk environments.								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Book Now 
					
					
				
								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
			
						
		
						
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
						
				
				
				
					## Course Overview
				
				
				
				
									The Advanced Fire Fighting course is a comprehensive training program designed to prepare fire wardens for workplace fire emergencies. It covers topics such as the Fire Tetrahedron, common causes of fires, fire prevention techniques, fire detection and methods of extinguishing fires through theoretical and practical components. The course also covers first aid techniques, emergency patient carry methods, fire risk assessment, and fire investigation and scene preservation. The aim of the course is to equip fire wardens with the necessary skills and knowledge to effectively respond to and prevent workplace fires while ensuring their own safety.								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
						
				
				
				
					Book Your Training Today
				
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
																														
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
							
                
                        
                            
                        
                        First Name*Email*
                            
                        Preferred Month for Training*JanuaryFebruaryMarchAprilMayJuneJulyAugustSeptemberOctoberNovemberDecemberPhone Number*Location*Johannesburg NorthCape TownDurbanPort ElizabethOtherThis field is hidden when viewing the formTraining RequiredreCAPTCHA
          
            
            
            
            
            
            
            
            
            
            
        
                        
                        

						
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
					### About the Advanced Firefighting Course
				
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
						
					
			
						
				
							
			
		
						
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
					#### Course Information
				
				
				
				
							
			
						
		
						
				
				
				
									**Duration**The Advanced Firefighting course is 2 days.**Cost**The cost of the course is R1.750.00 (exclusive of PPE and venue hire) exclusive of VAT.**Certification**Upon successful completion of the 2-day course, delegates will be awarded a certificate that is valid for a period of 2 years.**Venue**Training can be held on-premises at your organisation with a minimum of 8 attendees, or at one of our designated training centres located in Johannesburg North, Durban, Port Elizabeth, or Cape Town.								
				
					
		
					
		
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
						
					
			
						
				
							
			
		
						
				
					
		
				
			
						
				
					What We Offer
				
				
				
				
							
			
						
		
						
				
				
				
					Course Content and Modules
				
				
				
				
							
							
										The Fire Tetrahedron and the components required to sustain combustion
									
								
										Common causes of fires in the workplace
									
								
										Identifying different types of fires
									
								
										Fire Prevention Techniques
									
								
										Various fire detection and reporting methods
									
								
										The different classes of fires
									
								
										The different types of fire equipment including fire extinguishers, Fire Hose Reels, Fire Hydrants and Fire Hoses
									
								
										Which fires are extinguished with which fire extinguisher
									
								
										Personal safety requirements and Personal Protective Equipment (PPE)
									
								
										Methods of extinguishing fires (Practical component)
									
								
										First Aid techniques for treating burns
									
								
										Emergency Patient Carry Methods
									
								
										Fire Risk Assessment and Hazard Controls
									
								
										Monthly Fire Checklist which the firefighter has to be complete
									
								
										Fire Investigation and Scene Preservation techniques
									
						
						
				
				
				
									The Advanced Fire Fighting course consists of a combination of theoretical and practical components to adequately prepare a fire warden for workplace fires. The practical component also includes:Fire extinguisher operation and the extinguishment of a fireThe correct use of a hose reel and the extinguishment of a fireFire hydrant operations and hand signalsFire hydrant hose drills and the extinguishment of a fireSmoke house (site dependent)								
				
					
		
					
		
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
					
						
				
					Ready to start your training?

## OHS Management Services - First Aid and Fire Safety

Source: https://firstaidfiresafety.co.za/ohs-management-services/

# **OHS Management Services**
The Occupational Health &amp; Safety Act mandates health and safety training as an employer’s legal obligation.								
				
				
					
				
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
			
						
		
						
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
						
				
							
						
				
				
				
					## We Offer Comprehensive OHS Management Services
				
				
				
				
									First Aid, Fire and Safety Training (FAFST) has a team of experienced Occupational Health and Safety (OHS) practitioners who can help organisations implement practical and successful OHS management systems in their unique work environments. This ensures compliance with the Occupational Health and Safety Act 85 of 1993 and its requirements.&nbsp;FAFST offers various services related to OHS management, such as:								
				
					
		
					
		
		
					
		
				
				
																														
				
				
		
				
				
					## OHS Management Services
				
				
				
				
									Our specialised OHS management services include a monthly recurring arrangement, where an OHS practitioner is assigned to visit the organisation each month for a day or another specified period. This service is designed to help establish and maintain a customised OHS management system, ensuring that the organisation achieves and upholds a positive status in OHS compliance.**Price and Duration:**R8,950.00 (ex VAT) per month (8 hrs)1 day (8 hours) a monthR14,000.00 (ex VAT) per month (16 hrs)2 days (16 hours) a monthR25,000.00 (ex VAT) per month (32 hrs)4 days (32 hours) a month 								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Contact Us
					
					
				
								
				
				
					
				
		
					
		
				
				
					## OHS Compliance Assessment
				
				
				
				
									Our OHS experts are equipped to perform an OHS Compliance Assessment that evaluates your existing OHS system. This includes reviewing OHS documentation, risk assessments, organisational structures, training procedures, equipment, and meetings among other elements. Following the assessment, we will deliver a detailed report outlining the organisation’s OHS compliance level as a percentage. This report will highlight areas that are both compliant and non-compliant with the OHS Act and regulations, municipal by-laws, and more. The findings will serve as a basis to strategically enhance the organisation’s OHS standing and compliance score.**Price:****Small:** R5,000.00 (ex VAT)**Medium:** R7,500.00 (ex VAT)**Large:** R12,500.00 (ex VAT)&nbsp;								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Contact Us
					
					
				
								
				
				
		
				
				
																														
				
				
					
				
		
					
		
				
				
																														
				
				
		
				
				
					## OHS Equipment Assessment
				
				
				
				
									Compliance with the OHS Act, municipal by-laws, and the SANS national building regulations is mandatory, and it requires that a business’s premises are equipped to meet specific OHS and emergency statutory demands. A FAFST servicing technician or OHS practitioner will come and evaluate your workplace environment. This assessment ensures that the necessary emergency and OHS equipment for compliance and emergency response is present. Note that the OHS equipment assessment solely catalogues the required equipment items and their associated costs, and does not serve as an OHS act compliance assessment.**Price and Duration:****Small R 1,500.00 (ex VAT)&nbsp;**min 2 Hrs site assessment&nbsp;plus R 750.00 every hour thereafter**Medium R 3,000.00 (ex VAT)&nbsp;**approx 4 Hrs site assessment&nbsp;plus R 750.00 every hour thereafter**Large R 6,000.00 (ex VAT)&nbsp;**1 day site assessment&nbsp;plus R 750.00 for every hour thereafter								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Contact Us
					
					
				
								
				
				
					
				
		
					
		
				
				
					## OHS Risk Assessment
				
				
				
				
									Effective management of OHS risks stands as a critical objective for any organisation. An OHS practitioner from our team will perform a comprehensive on-site risk assessment at your facilities. This process focuses on identifying and cataloguing each potential hazard, along with its risk level. We will produce a detailed report, both written and photographic, that should be utilised by your management team to formulate a risk management strategy. This strategy should aim to either eliminate or reduce each identified risk. Conducting this OHS risk assessment annually is ideal and plays a vital role in fostering a workplace that is healthy, safe, well-prepared, and compliant.**Price and Duration:****Small size or Low Risk:&nbsp;**1-day R8,750.00 ex VAT&nbsp;(½ day assessment, ½ day report)**Medium size or Medium Risk:**&nbsp;2-days R15,000.00 ex VAT&nbsp;(1 day assessment, 1 day report)**Large size or High Risk:&nbsp;**3-days R22,500.00 ex VAT&nbsp;(3 days) + additional cost per day as required R 7,500.00&nbsp;								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Contact Us
					
					
				
								
				
				
		
				
				
																														
				
				
					
				
		
					
		
				
				
																														
				
				
		
				
				
					## OHS Files
				
				
				
				
									We offer support to your organisation in developing a current and accurate OHS file. This file will encompass a range of generic OHS documents that feature your company logo. Included within these standard OHS files are documents such as an OHS policy, evacuation policy, OHS organogram, appointment letters, OHS check sheets, and records of committee meetings, including agendas and minutes, among others.**Price:**R 7,500.00 (ex VAT)								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Contact Us
					
					
				
								
				
				
					
				
		
					
		
				
				
					Evacuation Drills
				
				
				
				
									Organisations must carry out evacuation drills twice a year to prepare their workforce for the potential occurrence of an emergency or disaster that would need an evacuation. AHS can dispatch a team to your facility to help organise a realistic emergency scenario and manage the evacuation drill. Following the drill, we will provide a report, both in writing and with photographs, that outlines the strengths, weaknesses, and recommended actions for improving the evacuation procedure and the subsequent drills.Price:**Small company:**&nbsp;2 x AHS evacuation marshalls @ R7,500.00 (ex VAT)**Medium company:**&nbsp;4 x AHS evacuation marshalls @ R12,500.00 (ex VAT)**Large company:**&nbsp;6 x AHS evacuation marshalls @ R17,500.00 (ex VAT)Thereafter an additional cost of R2,500.00 per AHS evacuation marshall								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Contact Us
					
					
				
								
				
				
		
				
				
																														
				
				
					
				
				
						
					
			
						
				
									The OHS Services listed above are an estimate and will be confirmed when our team has discussed your requirements in more detail.All prices are exclusive of VAT, travel &amp; accommodation								
				
					
		
					
		
				
						
					
			
					
						
				
					Ready to start your training?
				
				
				
				
									Download our course guide to view all course information and pricing.								
				
				
				
									
					
						
									Download schedule
